Eggeling
  1. For now Praj─Бpati, having gained his end, thought himself quite perfect. Establishing himself in the quarters he went on ordering (or creating) and disposing everything here; and inasmuch as he went on ordering and disposing, he is the Orderer. And in like manner does the Sacrificer, establishing himself in the quarters, order and dispose everything here.

Eggeling
  1. And, again, as to why he offers the Vai┼Ыvakarmaс╣Зa (oblations) 34. For the fire-altar there is both a beginning and an end: the S─Бvitra 35 (formulas) are the beginning, and the Vai┼Ыvakarmaс╣Зa (oblations) the end. Were he to offer only those to Savitr╠е, and not those to Vi┼Ыvakarman, it would be as if he made only a beginning and no end; and were he to offer only those to Vi┼Ыvakarman, and not those to Savitr╠е, it would be as if he made only an end and no beginning. He offers both of them, and thus makes both a beginning and an end.

тАж

Eggeling
  1. Having given a name to him, he reverently approaches him; for this (Sacrificer) builds him with his (own) whole self, and were he not to give utterance now to this surrender of his own self, he (Agni) would now take away his (the Sacrificer’s) self; but when he now gives utterance to this surrender of his own self, he (Agni) does not take away his self. [He approaches the fire] with the Anushс╣нubh verse (V─Бj. S. XVIII, 67), ‘What fires of the five races of men there are upon this earth,–thou art the chiefest of them: quicken us unto life!’–the Anushс╣нubh, doubtless, is speech, and all the metres are speech 44: he thus makes amends to him (Agni) by all the metres. Having stood by the fire, and lifted 45 it, and churned it out, he offers the completing oblation 46.

Eggeling
  1.   1. And, indeed, he who carries about Agni 57 becomes pregnant with all beings, and with all the gods; and he who builds him when he has not been carried about for a year kills all beings in the form of an embryo. But, surely, he who kills a human embryo, is despised, how much more then he who kills him (Agni), for he is a god: ‘Let no one become an officiating priest for an (Agni) who has not been carried about for a year,’ said V─Бtsya, ’lest he should be a participator in the killing of this, a god’s seed 58!’

Eggeling
  1. And, indeed, let him by all means build who was born a year (after conception); for Agni is the breath; it is thus him (Agni) he holds. And, indeed, as the breath, he enters into the infused seed, and takes possession of it; and inasmuch as he takes possession (vid) of every one that is born (j─Бta), he is J─Бtavedas. Wherefore by all means let even one who knows this build him as one ever carried (within him). And, indeed, if one who knows this either drinks (Soma), or offers drink to any one else, these libations of his will be offered even as would be his libations, when offered on a complete ┼Ъ─Бс╣Зс╕Нila fire-altar built up with wings and tail.

The term signifies ’the formula (yajus) of the completed offering (samishс╣нa).’ ↩︎

  23. 263:4 The four logeshс╣нak─Бs (clods of earth), being placed at the ends of the two ‘spines,’ represent the four quarters, marking as they do the centre of the east, south, west, and north sides of the altar-site, sown with seeds of all kinds; see VII, 3, I, 13 seq. The bunch of Darbha grass, placed in the centre, would thus represent the fifth region, viz. the one above. ↩︎

  24. 263:5 Though the Pr─Бс╣Зabhr╠еts are said to represent, not the regions, but the (channels of the) vital airs, they are placed in rows along the diagonals of the square body of the altar, thus marking, as it were, the intermediate regions; whilst the fifth set is placed in a circle round the centre.   57. 272:2 During the time of initiation (d─лksh─Б), which, if at all possible, is to last for a year, the Ukhya Agni has to be carried about by the intending Sacrificer, for at least part of each day, in the fire-pan (ukh─Б), suspended in a sling from his neck; the pan-fire being afterwards transferred to the newly built G─Бrhapatya and thence to the great fire-altar, to serve as the Citya Agni, or the ─Аhavan─лya fire. See VI, 7, I, 12 seq. ↩︎

  58. 272:3 In the original this last clause is in the first person,, or in the oraс╣нio с╕Нirecс╣нa, from the point of view of him who is asked to officiate as a priest, hence–Let no one become an officiating priest . . ., thinking, ‘Lest I should be a participator . . .’ ↩︎

  59. 273:1 That is to say, he must have been carried about for at least six months; and embryos less than six months old cannot live. ↩︎ ↩︎

  60. 273:2 This is so for the reason that the Mahad uktham consists of more than the eighties of verses; see IX, 3, 3, 19. One might feel inclined to include this whole sentence in the preceding quotation. ↩︎

  61. 273:3 That is, already too much attenuated, by being made as large as one a year old (?). ↩︎

  62. рдХрд╛с│ШрдордиреНрд╡рд╛с│Ш ABC. ↩︎

  63. 273:4 S─Бyaс╣Зa remarks, that this reply does not restrict the building of the fire-altar to one who has carried the fire for a full year, but only discountenances the building in the case of one who has only carried it for a few days (?). ↩︎
